Fire at the Continental Arcade 146

Carelessness by the Engineers' Society

Valuable Books Suffered Great Loss

A fire broke out at the Chinese Engineers' Society, room 542, on the fifth floor of the Continental Arcade on Nanjing Road, at 6:30 AM yesterday morning. Zhou Kui, a tea boy (24 years old, from Jinshan) who worked at the society, had already gotten up and gone to wash his face and use the restroom. When he returned to the room after finishing, he saw smoke billowing and flames blazing. Realizing that carelessness had caused the fire, he immediately ran out and reported it to the Central Patrol Station and the Fire Brigade, who dispatched vehicles to the scene. When the fire engines arrived at the Continental Arcade on Jiujiang Road, they did not know which section of the building had caught fire. After inquiring, they learned it was on the fifth floor. However, because the society was located very high, the water pipes had to be wound up the escalators, requiring a lot of time, causing the fire to rage fiercely. Fortunately, with the efforts of the firefighters, the fire was extinguished in about half an hour. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency went to investigate. Qiu Xie jun, the secretary-general of the society, had already arrived after hearing the news. He said that the society was formed by the merger of the former Chinese Engineers' Society and the Chinese Engineering Society. The president is Xu Peihuang, the current director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, and the vice president is Yun Zhen. There are over two hundred members who usually discuss engineering issues. They also have thousands of valuable reference books on chemical engineering, mining engineering, mechanical engineering, and other subjects, as well as hundreds of new books on reinforced concrete published by the society itself, stored upstairs. All of these were destroyed in the fire, which is a great pity. Many of the reference books were unique copies, difficult to collect, and given by engineering societies from various countries, which the society greatly valued. Therefore, they had insurance coverage of 8,000 yuan from the Dahua Insurance Company on Beijing Road. However, he did not know how the fire started because he had not witnessed it. He said that only a Zhou-surnamed worker stayed in the society and was usually careful and did not smoke. The total amount of the loss could not be estimated at the time. Xu Peihuang, the president of the society, also personally visited the scene after the incident.

Gong Shaoting's Murder of His Mistress Case 147

The Trial Concluded Yesterday, Sentencing Scheduled for the 9th

The key suspect in the sensational Jia Bei dismemberment case, Gong Shaoting, and his mistress Gong Hou, out of jealousy, strangled his former mistress Xie Aiqiao in the middle of the night, then cut off her head, and buried her body at the old site of Gong Hongtai Construction Factory, formerly run by Gong Shaoting on Gongxing Road in Zhabei, under the newly built bungalows. After the incident, only the headless body was recovered; her head has not been found. Gong Hou, who initiated the crime, Gong Shaoting, and Zhou Baoquan and Li Baosheng, who helped move the body, were successively arrested by the detective team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. They confessed to plotting to kill Xie Aiqiao and revealed that a fugitive accomplice, Shen Fufu, was still at large. They were transferred to the local court as ordered. Prosecutor Lei Binzhang interrogated the two suspects, Gong Shaoting and Gong Hou, for premeditated murder and destruction of a corpse, which violated Article 284, paragraph 1, clause 1, and Article 262, paragraph 1, of the Criminal Code. Zhou Baoquan and Li Baosheng were charged with abandoning a corpse, which violated Article 262, paragraph 1. A public prosecution was filed. Judge Zhang Shao once opened a trial, during which Gong Shaoting and Gong Hou recanted their previous confessions and denied everything. The judge ordered a further hearing. It is now learned that this case was reopened in the Fifth Tribunal yesterday morning at 10:00 AM by Judge Zhang Shao. The plaintiff, Xie Baolin, retained lawyer Song Shixiang to appear in court and request private compensation of 6,000 yuan. Gong Shaoting, Gong Hou, and others retained three lawyers, Peng Qixiu, Pan Zhenya, and Wu Xigong, who appeared in court to defend them. After the judge took the bench, he first called the plaintiff, Xie Baolin, to the case and asked, "During the last hearing, you said that Chen Zhangzhang informed you about Xie Aiqiao's murder. Therefore, you were ordered to invite Chen Zhangzhang to court. Has Chen Zhangzhang come today?" Xie replied, "I don't have a deep relationship with Chen Zhangzhang. We only met while drinking tea at the same teahouse. He certainly told me about this matter, but I haven't seen him come to drink tea for a long time, so there was no way to invite him." The judge asked, "How much private compensation are you requesting?" Xie replied, "Six thousand yuan." The judge ordered Gong Shaoting to be brought to the case and asked, "Does the deceased have any relatives? She only has an older sister, no one else." The judge asked, "Where are you from?" Gong replied, "Gaoqiao, Pudong." The judge asked, "During your previous confession, you said that when the deceased ran away, you went to Suzhou. Why did you say you went to the countryside in the reward notice? It's clear that your statements are inconsistent. Where were you at that time?" Gong replied, "I really went to Suzhou on business because I took on construction work in Suzhou, so I often went there." The judge asked, "You clearly confessed to the Public Security Bureau that Xie Aiqiao was murdered by Hou and your son-in-law Shen Fufu, etc." Gong replied, "It's a miscarriage of justice. I couldn't bear the suffering and confessed randomly." The judge said, "Then how is it that the place you indicated matches the place where the body was found, which is completely consistent with the facts?" Gong was speechless. Next, Gong Hou was brought to the case. The judge asked, "Why did you murder Xie Aiqiao?" Gong replied, "That is not the case." The judge asked, "You confessed very clearly in the Public Security Bureau. Are you still trying to quibble?" Gong replied, "It's a miscarriage of justice." After receiving the confession, the judge ordered Zhou Baoquan and Li Baosheng to be brought to the case. They both testified that they were ordered by the boss to move the remains, and they did not know anything else. At this point, prosecutor Lei Binzhang rose and argued, stating, "The murder of Xie Aiqiao has been around two years now. According to Zhou Baoquan, Gong Shaoting spent sixty yuan to hire people to dig up the body and rebury it elsewhere. Because the smell was offensive, Li Baosheng and others only moved the head. It can be said that the net of heaven is wide, and none can escape. When committing the crime, they first strangled her with a rope and then cut off her head. At that time, the neck blood had not yet congealed. According to the confession, Shen Fufu and a worker killed her. Moreover, according to Gong Shaoting's confession, because the deceased was tyrannical, the workers harbored resentment and plotted to harm her. Afterwards, Gong posted a notice stating that the deceased had run away, and then ordered Zhou Baoquan and others to dig up the body and rebury it elsewhere. This kind of evidence shows a strong suspicion of conspiracy. As for Zhou Baoquan, Li Baosheng, and others, they confessed to moving the body, and they only moved the head. Moreover, according to the Forensic Research Institute, the head was cut off not long after the strangulation. Please deliver a public verdict." The judge then ordered the start of the debate. The lawyers rose one after another and argued eloquently for a long time. As a result, the judge asked Gong Shaoting if he had a final statement. Gong replied, "My woman (referring to the deceased) is named Xie Aiqiao, also called Xie Baolin. There is also Xie Baolin's name on my sachet. Why is Xie Baolin now suing me? Isn't this a strange thing?" After receiving the confession, the judge considered the conclusion, scheduled the sentencing for 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month, and ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody pending the decision.

Special Feature: Discussion on Sino-Japanese Economic Cooperation (Continued) 152

— Mu Ouchu

Japan's export trade is the lifeblood of its economy. Today, Japanese goods are encountering resistance everywhere, so it has no choice but to turn to China. Moreover, the Chinese market has always had a very close relationship with Japan. The following is a list of Japan's foreign trade in 1930:

Japan's Export Trade to Various Countries in 1930 (Unit: 1,000 Japanese Yen)

Country Value Percentage

China 403,852 27.43

United States 506,112 34.43

European Countries 125,368 8.52

Other Countries 435,060 29.59

Total 1,469,858 100

The reason why we use the figures from 1930 as a standard is because at that time, Japan had not yet launched a military invasion to occupy our four northeastern provinces, and Sino-Japanese trade was in a normal state. But from the table, US-Japan trade is still above China. However, the US-Japan trade is mostly raw silk. Japan's export of raw silk to the United States accounts for 27 percent of its total exports and 96 percent of Japan's total raw silk exports. If Japan loses the US market, except for the silk industry, other industries will not be affected in any way. If it loses the Chinese market, Japan's entire industry will suffer a great blow. Former Yixing County Magistrate Arrested in Shanghai for Embezzling 20,000 Yuan in Public Funds 153

After Years of Secret Investigation, He Was Finally Arrested Recently

The First Special Court Approved His Transfer to the Jiangsu Provincial Government

Zhou Yanan, a native of Hunan, 46 years old, once held a position in the military and was later transferred to serve as the county magistrate of Yixing County, Jiangsu. He was dismissed from his post in January 1928. After an investigation by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it was discovered that Zhou had embezzled as much as 20,000 yuan in public funds during his tenure. The provincial government sent personnel to secretly investigate Zhou's whereabouts, but for many years, they found nothing. The provincial government issued a wanted notice in the newspapers. Recently, it was discovered that Zhou Yanan was hiding at number 35 Puqing Lane, Malan Road, in the French Concession of Shanghai. The provincial government sent a representative, Wang Ziying, with documents to Shanghai. Around 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, he encountered Zhou on Weihaiwei Road in the Public Concession. He had Chinese detective Sun Jishan and Chinese constable number 2587 take Zhou to the Chengdu Road Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was transferred to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, and lawyer Fan Gang, retained by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, applied for permission to transfer him, and police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that this case was one of assistance. Since Zhou was taken into custody at the police station, he admitted to owing only 2,000 yuan. Therefore, the Municipal Council did not oppose the transfer. Subsequently, Wang Ziying submitted official documents stating that he was a member of the Department of Finance and, after discovering that Zhou owed 20,000 yuan in public funds during his tenure, had been issued a wanted notice by the provincial government. Therefore, he requested the transfer. When questioned, Zhou Yanan stated that during his tenure, subordinates had been harmed by the Communist Party, so he spent 2,000 yuan on medical expenses, which he had reported to the provincial government for approval. After being dismissed, he went to Guizhou to handle affairs, etc. Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the statements and ordered that Zhou Yanan be allowed to be taken back for trial by the staff of the Jiangsu Provincial Government.

Conclusion of the Case of Han Yun'gen's Son's Engagement to a Dancing Girl 154

Lawyer Yang Qingyuan Testified in Court Yesterday

Stating That He Was Not Drunk or Confused When Signing the Contract

Han Yun'gen, a native of Ningbo who once served as the president of a certain bank, is known for his wealth. After resigning from his position as president, he switched to various other businesses. His adopted son, Han Peixian, is young and romantic and particularly fond of singing and dancing. Every evening, he would frequent various dance halls. Wang Xiaomei, the dance queen of the Great Shanghai Dance Hall, had a specially made small coffin carried to her home as a gift last summer, using it as a gimmick. Her fame increased as a result, and Peixian became even more enamored of her and grew closer. By last summer, their love had reached a boiling point, and they vowed to grow old together. On May 29th, they went to lawyer Yang Qingyuan's office to sign an engagement contract, specifying that they would marry within the year. If they failed to do so, Peixian would pay a penalty of 10,000 silver dollars. Later, Han Yun'gen learned of this and hired a lawyer to publish a statement in the newspaper and to prevent his son's dissolute behavior. Therefore, Peixian did not fulfill the contract, and Wang Xiaomei filed a lawsuit for breach of contract and damages. Since the contract was signed, not only did Xiaomei reject proposals from other men, but she also retired from her dancing career. Last month, the First Special District Court summoned both parties for questioning and ordered Han Peixian to negotiate a settlement with the plaintiff out of court. However, the defendant has not yet complied and has not expressed any willingness to resolve the matter peacefully, apparently because his father, Han Yun'gen, has not given Peixian the money, making it impossible for him to approach the other party. Yesterday afternoon, the date for the continued hearing arrived. The defendant, Han Peixian, knew that he was wrong and avoided appearing in court. His defense lawyer was also absent. Only the plaintiff, her lawyer, and the witness Yang Qingyuan appeared in court. Judge Peng ordered Yang to testify regarding the circumstances of signing the engagement contract. Lawyer Yang stated that Han Peixian and Wang Xiaomei came to his office on Avenue Edward VII that day and requested that he draft an engagement contract. At the time, Han Peixian was of sound mind and was not drunk or confused. The content of the contract was dictated by Han, and he wrote the draft according to Han's intentions. After Han reviewed and approved it in detail, he corrected it and wrote it in triplicate. Han and Wang each took one copy, and the remaining copy was kept in his office. He repeatedly asked about his ability to pay the 10,000 tael penalty specified in the contract in case of breach. Han firmly stated that he had assets and did not need to worry. He personally witnessed them sign and also signed as a witness. The plaintiff's lawyer then stood up and claimed that the defendant's father, Han Yun'gen, had already agreed to give him 800,000 in property and had already specified the types of property. Therefore, he was not concerned about the small amount of damages in this case. Judge Peng stated that the facts of the case were clear, and the defendant was absent without reason. He ordered the plaintiff to begin the final arguments alone and ordered a postponement for sentencing on a set date.

Li Gongying vs. Zhang Yingda Shanghai Billiards Final 155

Li Scored 222 Points More Yesterday on the First Day

The Final Victory or Defeat Depends on Today's Two Matches

The Shanghai Amateur Class A Billiards Competition is attended by famous Chinese and Western billiards players from all over Shanghai. The outcome determines who receives the championship, which is respectfully called the Shanghai Billiards King, truly deserving the title. In the past, those who competed for this throne were our country's Li Gongying and the Portuguese Mydina. This year is different. Mydina, who was said to have the highest hopes, was defeated by our country's famous player Zhang Yingda. Yesterday's final showdown was between our country's Li Gongying and Zhang Yingda, which is unprecedented in this competition and something to be proud of.

First Day's Progress Towards the Championship

The final totals 2,000 points, divided into two days, with 1,000 points each day. Yesterday was the first day, starting at 5:30 PM at the Victoria Recreation Club. Since defeating Mydina, Zhang has been in the limelight. Sure enough, within the first ten shots, he took the lead, somewhat able to compete with Billiards King Li Gongying, and remained in the leading position. Unexpectedly, he suddenly stopped at 355 points. At this time, Li Gongying was lagging behind at 305 points, taking the opportunity to score consecutive big numbers, such as 67 and 76, and soon caught up with over a hundred points, ending the first round with 500 points compared to 393. The second round started at 9:00 PM. Li Gongying's performance was more brilliant than before. Although Zhang tried his best to resist, he was no match for the old hero. Throughout the competition, Li's experience was rich, and he was able to give full play to his skills. However, in terms of individual performance, Zhang has made clear progress. Li is not as perfect as last year.

Let's See Who Wins Today

After the first day's result, Li won with 1,000 points compared to 778. There are two more final rounds today. According to observations from all sides, Li can still maintain the title of Billiards King. But a scholar who has been away for three days should be looked at with new eyes. Zhang has already been able to defeat Mydina, who knows if he can overcome Li Gongying? Looking at the first thirty shots before the first round yesterday, Zhang was indeed ahead of Li. Therefore, although there is hope, he must work harder. The highest scores of the two yesterday are as follows:

A Record of the Liangjiang Women's Basketball Team's Philippine Tour (1) 162

A Resounding Victory Over Central in the First Match: 49 to 13

Philippine Dispatch: The Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School basketball team's southern tour since arriving in the Philippines on February 11th has been warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese. Coincidentally, the Xiamen Qunhui team also arrived in the Philippines at the same time. The enthusiasm of the Philippine sports community is unprecedented in recent years. In several clashes, Liangjiang has won every time. People on the Philippine Islands have long admired Liangjiang's reputation and are eager to see their skills, so the stadium is packed with spectators for every match, creating a scene of everyone emptying their homes. Besides the arrival in the Philippines,

Luggage Just Unpacked, Warm Welcome

Various groups on the Philippine Islands, after learning about the arrival of the Liangjiang team, went to the port to greet them. At 3 PM on the 11th, when the President Jefferson approached the Manila pier, the Liangjiang students were all wearing snow-white domestically produced silk cheongsams, with short hair and extremely strong bodies. They lined up neatly, leaning against the ship's railing, waving flags and hands with those welcoming them. Dozens of groups, including the Overseas Chinese Sports Association, the Consulate General, the General Chamber of Commerce, the YMCA, the Party Headquarters, and newspaper offices, sent representatives on board to greet them. The hosts and guests shook hands with great enthusiasm. The Sports Association provided vehicles to transport all the luggage to the villa of Yang Qitai, the president of the Association, for accommodation. The villa has everything, including a gymnasium, tennis court, volleyball court, basketball court, music room, and reading room. Living there is very comfortable. There are a total of five Chinese newspapers in the area, as well as more than ten Western and Philippine newspapers. Reporters from each newspaper rushed to gather news and published special welcoming supplements to promote the event widely. The Overseas Chinese Sports Association is fully responsible for the reception, and a reception committee has been formed, with Yang Yongbao as the director, Ke Xiaoyun as the economic section chief, Chu Yongrong as the social section chief, and committee members Madam Yu, Ms. Yang Wenbi, Ms. Fu Shuzhen, Yang Jindeng in charge of catering and accommodation, Li Huancai in charge of the venue, Chen Daozhen in charge of publicity, Yang Yongbao in charge of competition, and committee members Yang Jindeng, Chen Zhang'e, etc., all dedicated to reception matters.

Miserable Defeat by the American Army in the First Clash

The competition matters are handled by the Philippine Overseas Chinese Sports Association. A total of four teams were invited: the American Central School women's team, the Philippine All-Star team, and the Xiamen Qunhui team, which won the Fujian Provincial Championship, for a double round-robin competition. Tickets were priced at 50 cents and one yuan. It started on February 15th. The first match was between Liangjiang and Central, held at the St. Thomas University basketball court at 7:45 PM. The referee was Bao Dishi, a former national athlete. Because of the reputation of both sides, the compatriots gathered enthusiastically. The entire Liangjiang team wore white shirts and green pants, looking refreshed. The entire audience applauded and welcomed them, and the atmosphere was very strong. During practice, their footwork was agile and their shots were accurate. The American team was all in white, with uneven builds. At 7:45 PM, the game began, and the audience's applause was thunderous. The Sports Association also temporarily organized a cheerleading team for Liangjiang, consisting of students from the Overseas Chinese Girls' School. At the start of the game, the beautiful women took the lead, scoring one point for Liangjiang with a free throw. After that, Chen Rongming scored six points in a row. Her speed in passing the ball and accuracy in shooting amazed the entire audience. After that, the momentum became one-sided. Liangjiang ended the first quarter with a score of 16-1. In the second quarter, Liangjiang's momentum continued, ending with a score of 29-3. With the victory in hand, Liangjiang called back its main players, Chen Rongming and Chen Jucai, and replaced them with Wang Shikun and Chen Meifeng, adopting a policy of passing without attacking. The American team took this opportunity to bring in the strong player Okika, and the momentum was indeed different. In addition, Pan Meng left the court due to cramps, giving the American army a chance to counterattack. In this quarter, the American army took the lead with 6 to 4. In the last quarter, Liangjiang brought back its main players, and finally won a great victory with a score of 49-13.

The Ministry of Education Investigates the Actual Situation of Handicrafts 166

(Nanjing, 4th dispatch) The Ministry of Education ordered all departments and bureaus that the "Procedure for Promoting Vocational Education in Provinces and Cities" promulgated by the Ministry requires attention to improving local existing handicrafts and using local existing enterprises or raw materials to develop new industries when each province and city decides to set up vocational subjects. The tables prepared last year, investigating the main raw materials, handicrafts, and established or planned vocational subjects in various provinces and cities for reference, have been mostly submitted and are being compiled for publication. In order to deeply understand the actual situation of the main inherent handicrafts in various provinces and cities, a survey table is specially issued, ordering the departments to fill it out in detail in conjunction with the Department of Construction, so that it can be compiled and distributed to various provinces and cities as a reference for the implementation of vocational education. As it concerns local vocational education, it is hoped that it will be completed and reported within two months of the arrival of the document for verification.

Hubei Education Department Formulates Literacy Education Plan 167

Utilizing Students

Eliminate Illiteracy

(Hankou Correspondence) The Hubei Provincial Department of Education, in order to eliminate illiteracy, will start with the provincial capital and formulate the "Outline of the Literacy Education Plan for the Hubei Provincial Capital," which is recorded as follows:

Organization

Utilize students from senior primary schools and above in the provincial capital to take turns teaching illiterate people aged ten to fifty in the provincial capital, so that they can read and exercise. (1) The Department of Education is responsible for organizing the Hubei Provincial Capital Illiteracy Elimination Corps, with the headquarters set up in the Department of Education, and the school as the unit, with branch headquarters set up in the school. (2) The headquarters of the corps will have one chief and one deputy chief, filled by the governor and the director of the Department of Education. Underneath will be two sections: administrative and supervisory, each with a director. Under the administrative section, there will be document, general affairs, accounting, and statistics groups, each with several staff members. The supervisory section will have several supervisors, assigned to each branch headquarters of the corps, responsible for inspection and guidance. The directors, staff members, and supervisors of each group will be concurrently appointed by the chiefs and deputy chiefs from the staff of various educational institutions. (3) Each branch headquarters of the corps will have several members, who will elect one chief and one deputy chief to be directed by the headquarters and the supervisor to preside over the affairs of the branch. The number of supervisors will be determined according to the standard of one supervisor for every ten members.

Zoning

The provincial capital will be divided into several teaching zones based on the number of schools, as the target of teaching. The size of the area will be determined based on the number of students and the size of each school. Zoning will be handled in conjunction with the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. Although there are no accurate surveys or statistics on the number of illiterate people in the provincial capital, it is estimated based on general academic principles that with a population of 300,000, there are approximately 180,000 illiterate people. Two terms will be divided each year, and each term is scheduled to teach 10,000 illiterate people, so that illiteracy will be eliminated in approximately nine years.

Members

(1) Each term is scheduled to have 3,000 members, initially filled by members of the youth service corps in each school, and then rotated with other students, so that each student can serve. (2) Members will take one to two hours each day to teach in the homes of illiterate people in the designated teaching area, and must teach at least three illiterate people, until the entire literacy textbook is completed. Illiterate people may be forced to attend school if necessary. (3) After a member identifies the illiterate people they are teaching, they will report to the branch headquarters, which will forward the report to the headquarters for record. (4) Members who are deemed to have excellent performance by the supervisor will be awarded prizes at the end of the term to encourage them. Those with poor performance will have their work grades in the school deducted as a warning.

Supervision

Each supervisor is responsible for examining and guiding ten members. The methods are: (1) Random supervision, with the supervisor supervising at any time at their discretion. (2) Regular assessment, with regular assessments when members have taught to a certain point, in order to change the curriculum. The curriculum is temporarily set to literacy, and the textbooks will be prepared and distributed by the headquarters.

Expenses

The budget is temporarily set at 9,000 yuan per term, provided by the provincial treasury. The budget is as follows: (1) Textbook fees: 24 cents per book per person per term, totaling 2,400 yuan. (2) Literacy certificate fees: 2 cents per certificate, totaling 200 yuan. (3) Prize fees: an average of 2 yuan per person, totaling 60 yuan. (4) Headquarters office expenses: 400 yuan per term.

London Art Exhibition British Commissioner Arrives in Beijing 168

Pre-exhibition in Shanghai to be Postponed

Method of Transporting to England Undecided

(Nanjing, 4th dispatch) Wang Shijie, director of the preparatory committee for the London Exhibition's review and re-selection of antiquities in Shanghai, previously dispatched Lei Zhen, director of the Ministry of Education, to Shanghai to assist in all matters. Lei returned to Beijing on the morning of the 4th. David and Raphael, the British commissioners sent to select and transport antiquities, also arrived in Beijing on the same train. Lei led them to meet with Minister Wang Shijie to discuss matters such as the safe transportation of antiquities to England. David and Raphael will stay for three or four days, visit President Wang, tour famous scenic spots, and then return to Shanghai. Lei stated that the review and re-selection of antiquities is being continued by the various preparatory committees in Shanghai. The pre-exhibition date, originally the 20th of this month, will inevitably be postponed if the selection cannot be completed by then. It has been decided that the exhibited antiquities will be transported to England in batches in June. Whether England will send a special ship to China for loading is currently undecided.

China Art Education Society Requests London Exhibition of Chinese Art 169

Proclamation Ensuring the Safety of Antiquities Sent Abroad

The China Art Education Society held its third regular board meeting at its clubhouse on Wenmiao Road yesterday. Executive directors Ma Gongyu, Yan Kechang, and Shi Chongpeng, directors Fu Boliang, Zhu Zhiwei, Wang Yunzhi, Shen Elou, Zhu Yunying, Shi Wenbin, and Zhang Chenbo attended. He Mingzhai and Mo Yunxuan were present as observers, and supervisors Chen Songchun, Ding Nianxian, and Wang Longzhang were present. Shi Chongpeng chaired the meeting, and Zhu Zhiwei recorded the minutes. The meeting began at 7:00 PM as usual. After the reports of each group's work were completed, discussions began on the compilation and publication of a weekly memorial issue to commemorate the founding of the society, as well as the holding of an exhibition. Regarding the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art, the selection of antiquities, and the long journey across the ocean, the board resolved to send a letter to the organizing committee requesting a clear proclamation to the people regarding the issue of ensuring the safety of the antiquities sent abroad, in order to dispel public doubts. Yan Kechang was immediately appointed to draft the letter, which was to be passed by the executive directors and then implemented. The society's letter to the London Art Exhibition is excerpted below:

Respectful greetings. Previously, the government, at the request of the British, selected antiquities to be transported to England for the International Exhibition of Chinese Art to be held in London in November of this year, allowing international audiences to gain a deep and widespread understanding of ancient Chinese art. The government's intention to promote national culture and foster Sino-British friendship is deeply admired by all our citizens. However, these rare antiquities are truly the essence of our Chinese nation's five thousand years of culture. In recent years, the nation's preservation efforts have not been fully adequate, resulting in either theft by corrupt officials or smuggling for profit by unscrupulous merchants. For example, the theft case at the Forbidden City remains unsolved, and we have not heard of the recovery of national treasures detained in Marseille. The continuous loss of protection has implications for the nation's fate, and thinking of this is deeply unsettling. The types and ages of the antiquities to be transported to England were specified by the British, and they also sent personnel to China to select them, which some observers believe undermines national dignity. Moreover, given the ever-changing international situation and the disparity in national power between our two countries, does our government truly have the confidence that it can ensure the safety of these numerous antiquities, the essence of thousands of years of national culture, during their long journey across the ocean, without any unforeseen risks? While it is said that there is legitimate insurance, how is its value assessed, and which country's company is underwriting this insurance? The government has not yet issued a clear statement on this matter, and the people remain deeply concerned. Therefore, while our society fully supports this grand exhibition, we cannot help but be overly concerned about the issue of ensuring the safety of the antiquities. Therefore, it is difficult to remain silent, and we hereby earnestly submit this letter, hoping that your committee will provide a concrete statement regarding measures to ensure the safety of the antiquities, and announce it to the public to clarify the situation and dispel public doubts. We eagerly await your response.

Industry Association and Machine Association Jointly Establish Industrial Management Training Class 175

The National Industry and Commerce Management Association and the Machine Association, recognizing the lack of industrial management talent in our country, have jointly established an Industrial Management Training Class. The first class of students graduated last winter, and registration for the second class will begin immediately. This year, the number of teaching hours will be increased to allow students to benefit more. The details are as follows: (1) Auditors: Factory directors and staff are welcome to join, with a limit of 40 participants. (2) Teachers: All will be experts in industrial and commercial management. (3) Curriculum: (1) Production Management (12 sessions), covering issues such as raw material procurement and management, machinery management, workflow, product inspection, and cargo management and transportation; (2) Accounting System (12 sessions), covering issues such as new accounting methods and the improvement of old-style bookkeeping and cost accounting systems; (3) Personnel Management (12 sessions), covering issues such as organization and authority, hiring, training, wages, benefits, and labor unions; (4) Marketing Issues (12 sessions), covering issues such as advertising, research, sales, agency systems, credit sales, and debt collection. (4) Duration: Classes will be held four times a week, two hours each time, with graduation after three months. (5) Reporting: Registration deadline is March 11th, and classes begin on the 18th. (6) Location: Inside the National Industry and Commerce Management Association, 146 Hardoon Road.

Page 12

Spring and Autumn

Snippets 177

— (Xiao Bai)

Watching the people on the trams, either crowding at the front to cool off, or tightly closing the doors to keep out the cold wind, one can tell that "spring" and "autumn" are changing.

The city is prosperous, and this year is "Children's Year" again. However, here, we see twelve- or thirteen-year-old boys pulling rickshaws, fourteen- or fifteen-year-old girls selling their souls, and a mournful cry of "selling children" echoing along the desolate streets.

Young people always want to transform society, but by middle age they only want to cling to it, and by old age they are afraid of even being able to hold onto it.

Mr. Qiu 178

— Qiu Zi

What kind of person is Mr. Qiu? Let me give a basic introduction.

Mr. Qiu is a young man in his thirties. Last winter, he came to Beijing with his new wife, Ms. Cai, intending to find a job in Beijing to serve society and the country. However, he had no influential relatives and was unwilling to be obsequious. He has been living idly in Beijing for almost two months, and the year has turned new, but he remains the same. Mr. Qiu does not adopt a passive attitude, which sets him apart from most young people today.

Mr. Qiu is a survivor of many battles, now unemployed for two months, becoming an "idle officer." His temperament can be described as "still as a virgin, swift as a hare." He is very fond of embroidery, saying that it is more interesting than any other pastime. In these two months, he has completed two pairs of embroidered pillows, with delicate craftsmanship and harmonious colors. My wife and neighboring women all praise him, calling him a "man of both literary and martial talents." I would rather call him a "man of both male and female talents." The ancient winter solstice poem says, "Who first notices the lengthening of the day by a thread? It is the embroiderers in the red boudoir." Now, even Mr. Qiu's footprints can be found in the red boudoir team, truly a lucky man!

He is also skilled in tailoring, sewing, mending socks, etc. When he has nothing to do, he often asks me, "Do you have any socks to mend?" which is very interesting.

Recently, Tan'er returned home for the winter vacation. Since I have to go out in the morning and afternoon, Mr. Qiu has become a genuine tutor, and sometimes he takes Tan'er to Nanjing Jimingsi Moqiu Lake to learn sketching.

Mr. Qiu has lived in my house for a full ten weeks. Now, Mr. Qiu has packed his bags and gone to the Lushan Military Training Corps. Spring returns to the earth, and a bright future awaits. I wish Mr. Qiu all the best for the country!

Landscape of the North Station 179

— Zhu Ying

The Shanghai North Railway Station, rebuilt after the January 28th Incident, is a rather magnificent fortress.

In this fortress-like station, countless people from the city to the countryside and from the countryside to the city are swallowed and spat out every day – people struggling on the lifeline.

Before each train departs, the travelers either have relaxed smiles on their faces or depressed expressions. After each train arrives, the travelers spat out by the train also have either relaxed smiles on their faces or depressed expressions.

On the platform, departing lovers often wave their handkerchiefs until the train has been dragged out of the platform. Indeed, the most unbearable thing in the world is parting. But at the moment the train arrives, the travelers who embrace their loved ones waiting on the platform, talking and laughing as they walk out of the station in pairs, that sweetness is so unforgettable.

In the waiting room, the rows of benches are always filled with people about to leave the city. However, there are also homeless wanderers, evicted by their landlords for not being able to pay the rent, spending the night in the waiting room.

Outside the station, countless rickshaws are always arranged vertically and horizontally, regardless of heat or cold, day or night, rain or shine. Each rickshaw puller is craning his neck, hoping to exchange labor for bread. Especially at the moment the train arrives, a trace of a smile will appear on everyone's sallow face.

Reading Paintings, Reading Poems 180

— Ding Min

Recently, the art wave of the great nation has been surging wildly. In Soviet Russia, Mei Lanfang, the handsome man, and Hu Die, the beautiful woman, along with the star representatives Zhou Jianyun and his wife, will be promoting Chinese drama and film art. In Nanyang, the venerable Zhang Shanzi has been entrusted by the Huang Society, and with his nephews, they will be exhibiting the multi-faceted artistic crystallization of Huangshan photography, poetry, calligraphy, and painting. In order to see it first, I rushed to Zhang's residence, and while they were checking and preparing for packing, I appreciated them piece by piece, roll by roll; at the same time, I quickly recorded several poems inscribed on Zhang's calligraphy and paintings.

Upon returning, I dare not monopolize the beauty, and I serve as a messenger, unconditionally transcribing three poems for everyone. You may wish to imagine yourselves as resurrected ancient poets and recite them aloud. The original poems are as follows:

(1) Huang Binhong's inscription: Broken walls and moss shadows dotted with cyan and purple, dug holes a thousand fathoms for guests' toes; looking down at the abyss, clouds are vast, wanting to cross but not crossing, the soul is frightened. Panting and sweating, grasping the cliff, gazing for a while, welcoming the west breeze to open the pale face; how I wish to sit here facing the mountain, spreading the pine green as a pu-cushion. Thoughts gallop endlessly, feet turn forward, experiencing danger and exhausting the secluded to greedily choose the best, the peaks rise from the ground competing for strangeness, allow me to slowly lead the drawing.

(2) Xu Shiying's inscription: I begin to believe that there is such a wonder in the world, Huangshan's years are leisurely; Tiandu and Lotus Peak view the majestic spirit, Yunggu and Lion Grove admire the beautiful posture. Heroes from the four seas now gather, the grand and the minute of a hundred years are exhausted; painting and writing are equally important, hoping to work together for the benefit of the country.

(3) Wu Hufan's inscription, Partridge Sky: Five hundred li of mountains are collected in a foot, white clouds sway and emerald peaks float; the scenery touches the heart and hurts the grey calamity, truly beautiful writing is used for traveling while lying down. Pines lead the guests, stones hide boats, visiting Zhang Hou at Qingliang Terrace, climbing three times to repeatedly carve, drawing and sketching the strange peaks.

News from Chaoshan Plum Blossoms 181

— (Fang An) (Bing Yu)

The news of Chaoshan plum blossoms is unparalleled. According to recent visitors from the mountain, I will report the following new information:

The Xianghai Building of Bao Ci Temple has recently been completed.

Winter is acting like spring, and the faint fragrance on the top of Qunyu Mountain is gradually floating, and the Song plums are blooming, like繁雪.

Haiyun Cave has recently been renovated, and a main road has been built for short stays in the mountain.

Famous artists from the sea, Wang Yiting, Yao Yuqin, Wu Dongmai, and Wang Geshan are currently taking pictures of the flowers, preparing to send them to the mountain to hang on the walls to add color to the mountain spirit.

Haiyun Cave and Qianyuan Guan preserve many local documents, among which Wen Zhengming's regular script Ding Gong tombstone and Liu Lan's statue are especially valuable, enough for those who love the ancient to appreciate and admire.

World Rare News

50,000-Year-Old Flea

In the Amber Quarry in Bielmigen, East Prussia, there is a piece of amber. An amber with a flea in it. According to archaeologists, it is from 50,000 years ago. The body of the flea is two grains of rice in size, so this piece of amber is considered a priceless treasure.

Humans at 150 Years Old

In the Moscow Institute for Life Extension, several scientists are working hard to study longevity methods. After research, it is found that humans can live to 150 years old. They have proven it with facts from the breeding period of animals to their growth status. The method of prolonging life is to inject endocrine fluid to supplement the function of metabolism, or to use blood transfusion procedures, or to use special nutrition methods, all of which can achieve the goal.

Comet Appears This Year

Mr. Jifia of the Lick Observatory in the United States has discovered that seven or eight comets will appear this year. Among them, the Lyende Comet will be clearly visible on May 2. As for the famous asteroid No. 944, it has not been seen for fourteen years, and it was discovered last October at the Simeiz Observatory in southern Russia. After passing through the perihelion, it is expected to appear in the sky again on March 5.

Hair Indicates Personality

There is a French-run barber shop in London. The barbers in this shop can distinguish the personality and physique of a person from the shape of their hair. Generally, the evaluations given at this barber shop are accurate. People with mental illness have a lot of messy hair. Impatient people have curly hair. People with dampness have dark, hard hair. Bald people are suspicious. People with miserable lives have dry, yellow hair. Honest people have soft, fine hair.

Accompany Mother to Prison for School

In the Sofia prison in Bulgaria, a widow was sentenced to ten months in prison. The woman has two daughters who are willing to live with their mother in prison. However, the two daughters are in school and requested the warden to allow them to attend school, so they went out early and returned late, until their mother's sentence was completed, when they were willing to return home with their mother.

Strange Storefront Decoration

There is a large jewelry store on Oxford Street in London. In its display window, there are jewels worth 20 million yuan. Hundreds of colorful jewels are embedded on the eaves of the window. However, to prevent thieves, dozens of petitioners are stationed outside the store day and night. It is truly the richest decoration in the world that has not been heard of.

New Modern Tax

Because of the poor local finances, Bulgaria has newly proposed several modern taxes. Generally, a woman is taxed two yuan for each hair perm. Women who draw eyebrows and apply lip makeup must pay three yuan per month to the police station in advance. Beautiful nails and powder cost three yuan per month. Women who beautify themselves without paying taxes, if they do not carry a tax certificate with them, will be charged double the amount if found. Since the implementation of the new tax law, women across the country are unwilling to beautify themselves. This is a new tax law that is stricter in prohibition than in levy.

Little Western Paradise 182

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 10 Indecent Lady In Front Show Wealth Selection Greedy Desire Wall Seam Inside Cause Injury Honest

Money, that kind of thing, can solve all the difficult problems in life. Everyone has a number of problems that need to be solved urgently, so you can't help but love money. If that person does not have superhuman reason, he will never be able to get money and not want it. As for those whose reason is not enough, as long as they get money, they can do anything. This cannot be blamed on people, it is forced by everyone's environment. At this time, Zhu Hu was at the end of her rope, even two or three copper coins could buy a piece of bread to fill her stomach, which was of great help to her. Now there are many foreign coins on the table. Zhang Jiefu said that as long as her mind moved, these foreign coins would be hers. After hearing this, she couldn't help but tremble all over and asked: Zhang Lao Ye, you...you...what are you talking about? Zhang Jiefu glanced at Yueying and continued: You are honest people, can I still deceive you with words? If you move your mind, these foreign coins will be yours immediately. Hu looked at the corner of the table and saw that even though the foreign coins were covered with paper, she could still see the white light shining outside. He said, if I move my mind, these foreign coins will be mine immediately. Could it be that he wants me to grab these foreign coins and run away? I can't even walk, how can I run? And this Little Western Paradise is very big. I came in and couldn't even tell east, west, south, or north. How can he let me run out? Thinking so, she supported the table, couldn't help but rise and fall three times, her eyes all shot at the corner of the table. Zhang Jiefu looked at her situation and couldn't understand what he meant, so he said: This sister-in-law, did you hear what I said? If you move your mind, these foreign coins will be yours immediately (148)

Imperial Incense Drifting Record 183

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

"Are they all on that side of the car?" She asked Li Lianying.

"They're all on the left, Empress Dowager!" Li replied.

The car was entering the station, and the speed had slowed to the lowest degree. The Empress Dowager slowly walked down from her throne, leaned against the left side of the car window, and faced outside. The rest of the people stayed in place and did not dare to act rashly. At this time, Guangxu was still in his own car; the Empress Dowager specifically told me to stand behind her - this position should have been Guangxu's. Of course, I was very happy to comply, and I was glad that my height was just a little taller than hers, so I could see everything outside clearly over her shoulder. The situation was exactly the same as what we saw when we came: many officials, a large team of soldiers, and the lanterns on the platform, nothing had changed; and Yuan Shikai himself was still kneeling slightly ahead of everyone, showing his identity as the leader. The Empress Dowager smiled slightly as she watched this moving scene slowly shifting in front of her; but the officials were lowering their heads to the ground, respectfully saluting her, so naturally they did not see her smile. Although I was standing behind her shoulder, I could still see it from the corner of her mouth; this smile was indeed extraordinarily gentle and loving, but it could not conceal her fatigue and exhaustion. The image I felt from her smile was indeed very profound and still lingers on my nerves.

Didn't it say in Chapter 14 of this book that Yuan Shikai had a Western orchestra that he brought to Fengtian with the Empress Dowager? At that time, it was said to be a temporary loan, so Qing Shan and his stewards had already thought about it, and they let Wu tell that group of Western orchestra to get off the train in Tianjin. (259)

Astonishing Low Price of 806 Yuan

The gold market was in utter chaos yesterday, with a turbulent day of extreme volatility. As the Legislative Yuan is discussing legislation detrimental to the silver standard, the long positions collapsed as expected. Once the selling began, the long positions were exhausted and unable to hold any longer, forcing them to liquidate in pain, leading to a break through major levels and the discovery of an astonishing new low price of 806 yuan. Afterwards, it stabilized slightly. Finally, Sassoon covered short positions, the foreign exchange market tightened, and the rebound was swift. It was noted that initially, overseas silver markets surged across the board, with London spot gold rising sharply by one shilling and nine and a half pence, leading to a further devaluation of the pound and a severe drop in exchange rates. However, it was generally expected that the silver market's rise was too rapid and might retrace, so the gold market might have a chance to rebound. As a result, off-exchange forward transactions opened, although low, not quite enough, initially around 40 yuan, then dropping to 33 or 34 yuan, then rebounding to 38 or 39 yuan. 紗花 186

Yarn and Cotton Appear to Be Recovering

The yarn market initially fell and then rose, but local market confidence showed a turning point, because it had been falling for many days, and recently spot yarn sales were still smooth and healthy, and there were also long position company organizations, so most people's sentiment saw a possibility of recovery. However, the international currency war is exceptionally fierce, which is very unfavorable to our country's commodity prices.

Free Talk

Urbanites' Worries and Joys 188

— Meng Jia

In these times, those who can truly "find joy in forgetting worries" are rare. Those who can are mostly people without "worries," or whose "worries" are not real worries. In the New Year, "we have merchants slaughtering livestock to welcome the God of Wealth; scholars gathering elegantly to celebrate the festival; heroes watching women set off firecrackers; onlookers standing by the roadside, clapping and cheering," as well as young gentlemen from wealthy families who frequent the dog racing track to bet on single winners and dance the Charleston at the Paramount. Do they really have any "worries"? Perhaps the troubles of jealousy in love, but these trivial "worries" can indeed be forgotten with "joy." If we were to blame them for forgetting the "national crisis" and for "forgetting the pain once the wound has healed"—especially since the wound hasn't actually healed yet—it would still be "alienating" them. Some of them still consider themselves "not lagging behind," because they actually do wear some "domestic goods." Besides, in reality, there isn't really any "wound" now.

"Finding a bit of happiness in forgetting the pain amidst suffering" can only be done by those who believe their suffering isn't that great, or those who have none at all, yet put on a face as if they are suffering. They have no suffering, or "their suffering" is minimal. After visiting the dog racing track once or twice, embracing a dancer, and being driven home in a car at three in the morning, they climb into bed and can forget everything by the next morning.

In the city, the silent weeping of those who have gone bankrupt and the forced smiles of those who are outwardly strong but inwardly weak, fearing that others will see their weaknesses, are indeed drowned out by the gentle singing of "Peach Blossom River, My Darling I Love You" on the radio and the boisterous laughter of the successful. As for the countryside, not only is there no Lantern Festival, there isn't even a "New Year." "Worries" exist, and they cannot be forgotten with "joy." Even if there is some "joy," it cannot stir up any happiness. Moreover, there isn't even "joy" enough to forget worries!

During the Lantern Festival, who has ever seen a beggar dancing the Charleston in an alleyway? Using "medicine to forget worries"? I have only seen "beggars" who have fled from bankrupt Jiangbei villages to this prosperous city, staring at elegant young women—but not to set off firecrackers, but to ask for a few coppers, only to receive a frown and a few cries of "unjust death"!

It is clear that those who "find joy in forgetting worries" are few and far between, and not something everyone can accomplish.

Again, "Essays" 189

— Lin Xijun

In reply to Mr. Tang Tao

Previously, I unintentionally wrote an essay titled "Essays and Essayists" (published in the "Literary Soliloquy" section of Modern Magazine in September of last year), expressing my humble opinion on this phenomenon—it was just a humble opinion, and I dared not presume it to be a profound theory. Unexpectedly, it stirred up public outrage, and I was attacked with both direct and indirect methods. I had not anticipated that my words would touch people's sore spots. The tense reactions of people were not without reason, and since I didn't have an organization to back me up, like "two people forming a faction, three people forming a clique," I could only let the "brave soldiers" stand alone and remain silent.

I thought I could finally have peace, but the flames of the "heroes" continued to spread, seemingly burning endlessly. During a forum in a certain major magazine, they seemed unable to forget this "hatred," continuously firing cold arrows at me.

Now I have to say something.

I had occasionally read an article by Mr. Tang Tao in Reading Life, titled "Essays and Cooks," which also used the cold arrow tactics commonly used by "heroes," firing several "poison arrows" at me. Now, in Free Talk, I see Mr. Tang Tao's "Talking About Essays." Mr. Tang Tao's repeated defense of essays suggests he is undoubtedly a "long live essays" advocate.

However, Mr. Tang Tao this time did not fully understand the original intention of my humble article "More and Less" in the recent Literary Pictorial, but only extracted fragments to use as ammunition for attack. I cannot agree with this attitude.

In my previous two short articles, I repeatedly said that "the essays currently popular touch on a wide range of topics, almost encompassing various social issues of current affairs, international affairs, and politics, almost no different from the commentary articles in newspapers." And as Mr. Tang Tao said, "essays are indeed not like novels, poems, or dramas." At the same time, they are no different from other non-literary works, such as various academic papers and narratives. It is impossible to force any "slight" literary nature onto them. But here I want to solemnly state that I am definitely not a formalist mechanist, and I never said that articles other than literary works such as novels or dramas are not needed. If they are not wasteful, they still have another aspect of meaning and effect. (Such as papers on politics, economics, and other categories.) This is like the prejudice expressed in the "forum" of a certain major magazine that "essays have taken on a particularly important responsibility in the past year," singling out essays as if the entire literary scene in the past year had nothing worth recording except for essays (in fact, essays cannot be considered literary works and regarded as the harvest of the literary scene). Isn't this obviously distorting the facts and having ulterior motives? It is true that "essays" have mysteriously flourished in the past year, but very few of them are well-written (if they have any value at all). If there are so-called well-written ones, I think they are probably just good at personal attacks. I don't believe there's anything great about that. Now that the call for great works is extremely loud, some people optimistically tell us that "it (referring to essays) is the era of quiet cultivation for the arrival of great works in the near future." Fortunately, "the near future" will "arrive," and we might as well be optimistic with the prophets and wait for the arrival of this great work in the near future. However, I always suspect that it is a kind of unlimited blank check.

I don't have the authority to stop "essayists" from burying themselves in the "era of quiet cultivation for the near future" for the work of "great works" that is "better" than everything else, nor do I have the great ability to extinguish these "very necessary" "essays." Mr. Tang Tao doesn't have to worry too much. Future events are difficult to predict, so let's wait and see.

City of Sin 190

— Li Sanlang

The early spring in Macau is so warm. The slight breeze caresses the hearts of travelers. The air is filled with a Western flavor! On the high, refreshing hills, beautiful houses are arranged, standing one by one on the sloping cement roads. In the spaces between the lush evergreen trees, one can vaguely see the red and green tiled roofs. Quietly, distantly, some small birds that are not afraid of the cold chirp, stirring my emotions:

Beautiful and lovely spring has arrived.

The market in Macau is always in a frenzy.

On the shore of the surging South Sea, the streets and alleys are filled with arrogant sounds. In the dimly lit gambling dens, countless people want to bury their dazed minds in the depths of white silver and colorful banknotes. When they reach the point where survival is impossible, they throw their lives into the raging waves, quietly. Then, batch after batch of gamblers with great desires squeeze in, struggling in the twisted circle of life from day to night, from spring to winter, endlessly.

There, although there is a deep sense of human sorrow, most people are reveling. The bare-chested, bare-armed courtesans have captivating bodies. They bewitch the young and the lovelorn who have been squeezed out of the circle of life. When the demon of money cruelly whips them, they put on a bitter smile, perhaps with a sorrowful sympathy, and send them into the emerald green waves. However, groups of men are then drawn into that fragrant environment. When they are plundered by the whips of life and can no longer survive, then a group of village girls quickly arrive, eternally sinking in the tragic march of revelry!

There are countless skeletons, forever buried in dark rooms, sucking the marrow of man-eating opium. There are high-ceilinged dance halls where people of authority dance until dawn, holding the slender waists of charming women.

But alas! City of sin! It is only a gathering place for disheartened wealthy people! Forever rolling and tumbling, one day it will be buried by the roaring seawater.

Talking About My Own Paintings 191

— Zikai

"Colored Zikai New Year Cartoons"

The Kai Ming Bookstore's "Middle School Student Magazine" included a color print of my vertical painting on Chinese paper, called "Colored Zikai New Year Cartoons," as a supplement to its January issue this year. When I saw this title on the advertisement, I found it funny because I was squeezed between two adjectives and placed on top of a noun, which felt a bit unnatural.

However, I dare not blame the unnaturalness of the title. Because my painting is more unnatural than the title. This vertical painting is simply wrong!

Tens of thousands of middle school student readers probably did not notice the mistakes in my painting. Otherwise, why have there only been letters in the past month or two asking me for paintings on rice paper, and no letters pointing out the errors in this vertical painting? Also, why would someone be willing to mount this painting, so that this erroneous painting would be displayed high on the walls of framing shops? But perhaps not: perhaps someone has already seen the mistakes in this vertical painting and is discussing them. However, they disdain, are unwilling, or find it inconvenient to announce them in writing to embarrass me.

But it seems I don't need a platform. I'm dismantling it myself here: This vertical painting is wrong; at least, it is very clumsily drawn. Let me confess:

Where is the mistake in the painting? Please look at the painting: In the foreground is the shore, and on the shore is a tall pine tree. In the background is also the shore, and half of a rising sun is emerging from the horizon, emitting light and driving away the clouds above. In the midground is a small boat, close to this shore, heading towards the rising sun on the other shore. The mistake is in this place. Please look at the boat: there are four people in total, two young men wearing Boy Scout uniforms, one sitting at the bow and one sitting at the stern. There are also two young women, sitting together in the cabin. They are all facing the rising sun, with their backs to the viewer; they are all rowing. The person at the stern is holding the middle of the oar with his right hand and the end of the handle with his left hand, using the oar as a rudder. The other three oars are all tied to the side of the boat in the middle. The three of them are holding the ends of the handles with both hands and pushing and pulling up and down. A friend told me, "You drew it wrong! These three are all rowing backwards, and the boat cannot reach the bright shore. Instead, it is retreating"! That's right, these three oars use the principle of leverage. The point where it is tied to the side of the boat is the fulcrum. The end of the handle is the force point. The oar blade in the water is the weight point. Pushing the oar blade into the water and pulling the handle, the boat will naturally move backwards, retreating and crashing onto this shore. This is a very big mistake.

However, I can argue: These three are all "pushing the oars," not "rowing the oars." When pushing the oar, when the oar blade enters the water, push the oar handle forward, and when it comes out of the water, pull it backward. The boat will also move forward. Pictures cannot show past and future actions like movies. How do you know that the young man leaning forward at the bow is not just finishing a push and is about to start pulling in an oar? How do you know that the two young women leaning back in the cabin are not just starting to push the oars and just finishing pulling in an oar?

My friend smiled and told me: "Your hands hold a pen all year round, and you have never held an oar. You don't know the joys and sorrows of this. This strong argument is clearly useless. Do you know that pushing the oar is very laborious and slow, and when pulling it in, the oar blade comes out of the water and is in the air, light and floating? If the body doesn't use force, it is easy to fall backwards. Smart boatmen would never use this method. Even if your words are correct, the young men and women in this boat are all clumsy people who "put in effort but get no results." I tell you, you should teach them to "turn around," facing the viewer and with their backs to the light. In this way, they can save effort, reach the destination quickly, and use smiling faces to please the viewer. Wouldn't that kill three birds with one stone!"

When I heard these words, I suddenly realized. The next day, I ran to the lake early in the morning, hired a boat, turned the bow towards the rising sun, and personally practiced this pushing the oars. Indeed, I felt it was very laborious, very slow, and if I didn't use force, it was very easy to fall over. Moreover, I was laughed at by the boatman, who advised me: "Sir, turn around and put your butt towards the sunlight. It's much more comfortable!" I once listened to his advice, but immediately turned around again, willing to put in effort but get no results. Because after being comfortable, I discovered a big flaw: I could no longer see the sun and turned my back on the light. There are no eyes on the buttocks, and my heart is always anxious, not knowing if my boat is heading straight on the path of light? Therefore, I would rather put in more effort, be slower, use more strength, and still take my rowing method. Let others laugh at my clumsiness. As long as I can face the light and move forward, my heart will be at peace. At this time, I realized two philosophical principles of rowing towards the rising sun: If you want to save effort, want to achieve it quickly, want to be comfortable, and want not to be laughed at, you must turn your back on the light. If you want to face the light, you have to put in a little more effort, be a little slower, use a little strength, and be laughed at a few more times.

Ah! This vertical painting of mine is wrong! I am sorry to the printers and the bookstore, who had to spend a lot of money to print and distribute it, but that is secondary. First of all, I am sorry to the readers: the painting clearly states "Made for middle school student readers on the first day of the twenty-fourth year," as if it is advising young people to put in effort, be slow, use strength, and be laughed at on New Year's Day, which is a time to wish for prosperity. This is such a big mistake! Because in the current world, practicality comes first, and everyone tries their best to save effort, achieve quickly, and be comfortable. Who would be willing to put in effort for some unattainable light and do things that don't pay off?

When this vertical painting was not yet printed, a well-meaning friend pointed out the factual errors in this painting. But I stubbornly refused to listen and published the painting. "Once a word is spoken, it is hard to undo." Moreover, tens of thousands of "Colored Zikai New Year Cartoons" have been delivered by postmen to the desks of tens of thousands of readers, and I don't even have a nag, how can I get them back? Let me be wrong to the end, clumsy to the end. Not only do I confess my mistakes and clumsiness here, but I also post an advertisement here to start selling my kind of wrong and clumsy paintings. This article can also be said to be an advertisement for the advertisement.

March 1, twenty-fourth year, No. 6, Huangqin Lane, Hangzhou.

Grandmother Selling Gold Ingots 192

— TK

Toward Evening (13) 193

— Qu Yi

"Haha!" Li An couldn't help but laugh at this statement, yet immediately, for some unknown reason, a wave of bitterness welled up in his heart. He threw the empty glass on the table and staggered to his feet, only to collapse back onto the sofa. "You little witch, you dare to be coy with me! I don't care about you! I!" As he spoke, white froth bubbled from his mouth, and he drifted back to sleep, snoring loudly.

"Loss of vitality! Loss of vitality," the New Literary Man muttered to himself, "This is a loss of national vitality. The Japanese would never get this drunk, unless it's the Cherry Blossom Festival! When I was in Japan!"

"Heh! Heh! What about me!" The big-bellied man's pumpkin face, resembling a smaller globe on a larger globe, was spinning now as well. "I also want! Hey, another drink. If this drink gets spilled too, then we're done for. Yi Yuan, have you calculated yet, how much profit we can get from this lottery, net of printing costs? As the saying goes, horses won't get fat without pasture, and people won't get rich without unexpected wealth. Nowadays, it's a dream to make money from legitimate businesses. Yi Yuan, what do you think? Speaking of my profession, people don't even have enough to eat, so who's wearing silver rings and using silver ear picks? When daughters get married, it's a giveaway; twenty years old, twenty dollars; hoping someone will foot the bill! So, in these times, I, as a division commander, have no taste for it anymore. You can forget about being promoted to army commander!"

Holding onto the table, he stood up, the table rocking from side to side, the dishes clattering. The big-bellied man retreated to the bed, sprawling out on his back, his belly sticking out.

The Sofa Walker, in his drunken dream, took the sound of the dishes to be some kind of music, waving his hand in revulsion, striking a Rodin-esque pose. "Good, good, dear girl! Do a waltz! I'll play the violin. Heh; heh! Zzzzzz..." He turned over and couldn't help but vomit.

"Joke! Joke!" Hu Yiyuan finally put down his chopsticks and stood up. "Can't handle it like that! Although I, Hu Yiyuan, am young, I've been through storms." Saying this, he pulled up the long sleeves of his short jacket to his shoulders.

The New Literary Man was quite moved. He seized the opportunity to add a critique: "Too pointless, too pointless!"

"But—I still want a melody of 'Flute at Yellow Crane Tower, Plum Blossoms Falling in the Fifth Month of Jiangcheng.' Don't think it's pointless! Heh..." Smiling, Hu Yiyuan squeezed into the bed.

Before the sound of smoking could be heard, Guo Ren was concentrating on an article on the prohibition of alcohol to save the nation. Suddenly, a flurry of footsteps arose outside the door—the sounds of leather shoes, cloth shoes, girls' laughter, and men's fake scolding—then the door creaked open again.

"Hu Yiyuan! Hu Yiyuan!"

"Young Master Hu! Young Master Hu!"

A man's voice that had been smoothed of its sharp edges and a woman's voice that scratched the nerves like a saw also came out at the same time as the opening of the door. Door.

A middle-aged captive in a gray suit was ushered in by a group of women soldiers—the faces of those women soldiers were all smeared with red, like overripe peaches.

The New Literary Man immediately darkened his face, retreating to the corner of the room at the same time.

"Ugh! Red terror! Red terror!" He muttered again to himself in a low voice.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Gandhi Opposes Old Man Marrying 194

— Ding

A Havas dispatch from the previous day stated that an old, wealthy Indian man in Mumbai, sixty years of age, will soon marry a thirteen-year-old girl. Mahatma Gandhi specifically telegraphed the National Congress to protest this matter, saying that it is inappropriate for an underage girl to marry an old man in his sixties. Gandhi also ordered his followers to find ways to resist this. Gandhi is truly a meddler, a master of pranks.

Indian women mature early by nature, and it is not uncommon for a thirteen-year-old to be a mother. Moreover, the old man is wealthy, so the girl is naturally willing to marry him. Even in terms of the law, it is legally permissible for a withered willow to bloom. Why should Gandhi bother to interfere in their happy event? It's like stirring up a pond of spring water, none of his business.

Even from the girl's point of view, it is not a bad move. A man can remarry after his wife dies, and a woman can naturally remarry after her husband dies. Although the laws of India have not been investigated, it is assumed that they are no different. Since this is the case, if the old man dies, the woman can remarry. Even if she doesn't want to marry, she will still have plenty of money and be a wealthy woman. She has a legitimate path to take, and there are many other flexible solutions, which need not be mentioned.

Gandhi is truly not a content and self-disciplined fellow, insisting on interfering and telegraphing the National Congress to express his protest. Not only that, but he also ordered his followers to find ways to resist, so that the white-haired and red-faced can consummate a good relationship. What is the reason for this? In 1931, a similar incident occurred. On the day of the wedding, Gandhi's followers organized a funeral procession, sending them off along the way and mocking them. Now, Gandhi's followers know that the old story will be repeated, and it remains to be seen whether they will come up with new tricks.

However, there are many extremely inhumane and unreasonable things in the world, which the law often cannot prohibit. In such cases, it is only possible to deal with them using extraordinary means. Gandhi is in a colony under the British Empire and cannot resist, so he can only promote non-resistance and non-cooperation as a way to deal with it. The imperialists have no way to control him. Now Gandhi is also using this method to interfere in the old man's marriage, which is truly the same technique.

I recall that during the Qing Dynasty, only those with rank could wear a full red cloak. A certain prefect, upon arriving at his post, saw that many members of the gentry in the area were wearing full red hats. However, these people were mostly members of the gentry, and he didn't want to seriously challenge them and order a ban, because the gentry class during the Qing Dynasty had a special kind of power that was not to be easily offended. This power still exists to a considerable extent today. The prefect came up with a plan and made hundreds of full red hats, distributing them to beggars, and the trend disappeared.

It can be seen that everyone knows how to perform magic tricks, and each has their own different skills. The world is full of unreasonable things, and there are unreasonable ways to deal with them. When the law loses its effectiveness, there are special methods to remedy it.

Letters from a Certain Person 195

— Xiao Hong

Friend, didn’t you say, “Although the environment makes you like this, you must take care of your health?” How are you now? A page full of gray, a page full of distress.

Speaking of which, my environment is much worse than yours, and my distress is heavier than yours, but I would rather deeply dam it in my heart. I will overcome it with the greatest strength. If a glimmer of hope hangs before me, I will grasp it with tears in my eyes and embrace my incomplete heart to march toward this hope. Although I have been severely hit many times, even this glimmer of hope cannot be realized.

Sometimes, I also have the same thoughts as you, like "How to be a person" and "What is life", but I often jokingly say, "It is for the lover's charming smile," "It is for the lover's..." and think it through.

Although, it’s a pity, I still don’t have a lover, but when I am distressed, I still often use this almost joking thought to heal my wounds and to encourage my remaining courage after failure.

Really, until now, on the one hand, I enjoy myself to the fullest, and on the other hand, I encourage myself even more. At least, I think, in this world, I still have myself who loves me, I am still young, and I still have things to do. Why should I be depressed? Why should I be depressed!

When friends see me enjoying myself to the fullest, they all say that I have changed. One friend even kindly said to another friend: "X, be careful of Xiao Hong's suicide. Look how badly he has changed."

When my friend told me this, I couldn't help but thank my friend for his kindness. At the same time, I felt greatly insulted. That friend who deserves my thanks underestimated me too much. He thought that after a few failures in the trenches of life, I would commit suicide behind people’s backs. He was even worried because he saw me enjoying myself to the fullest recently. Friend, I will not commit suicide. I may kill someone, or I may be killed, but I will never end my own life with my own hands.

If you say that my enjoying myself to the fullest is practicing "chronic suicide," then I want to ask: When suffering constant blows, isn’t a person allowed to use entertainment to relieve temporary pain? Isn’t a person allowed to use entertainment as a marching song for their career? If not, please seal the mouths of manual laborers. Aren't they humming "Hang yo! Hang yo!" when they work?

You said that your friends have become indifferent to you, and that you still regret that you have lost the love of many friends in exchange for one person’s soul. You seem to feel the narrowness and pain of this world.

Friends are indifferent to you, perhaps it is your overthinking, but perhaps it is true. However, why should friends be indifferent to you? Are they disappointed because you gained a soul? It is truly something to congratulate yourself on when such friends leave. Why feel depressed again? As for other friends who seem to be estranged, you also feel the sadness of being separated from the group. In fact, haven’t you already said, "The closeness of friends is not built on the closeness of interaction?"

Friend, don't be so sickly sentimental. Comfort yourself. Find something to relieve your distress. In this era, in this world, who among us doesn’t have a belly full of distress?

Besides, you still have a "soul" that you have obtained. Take a step back and think, what if you lost even this "soul"? There are many people in this world who live empty and hollow!

Friend, think about yourself tomorrow and throw away those sorrows like you would discard a cigarette butt.
